  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de8e2427-d6f3-4578-87b8-ec318d823251'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText12604532106147946370" style="display:none">Can Sloane and James survive the lies and secrets surrounding them, or will The Program claim them in the end? Find out in this sequel to The Program, which Publishers Weekly called “chilling and suspenseful.”<br /><br />How do you stop an epidemic?<br /><br />Sloane and James are on the run after barely surviving the suicide epidemic and The Program. But they’re not out of danger. Huge pieces of their memories are still missing, and although Sloane and James have found their way back to each other, The Program isn’t ready to let them go.<br /><br />Escaping with a group of troubled rebels, Sloane and James will have to figure out who they can trust, and how to take down The Program. But for as far as they’ve come, there’s still a lot Sloane and James can’t remember. The key to unlocking their past lies with the Treatment—a pill that can bring back forgotten memories, but at a high cost. And there’s only one dose.<br /><br />Ultimately when the stakes are at their highest, can Sloane and James survive the many lies and secrets surrounding them, or will The Program claim them in the end?</span>

  <span id="freeText18151634109112595580" style="display:none"><i>Huge thank you to the publisher for letting me read this advanced copy. I loved the tone, the characters, the issues that it dealt with... but wow. WOW. This book was just... wow. Basically the book starts up where the last one left off, and Sloane and James are on the run. They IMMEDIATELY get picked up by "the rebels" (there are two of them) who take them to a safe house and they meet up with Lacey. Lacey is having recall problems and like THE NIGHT Sloane and James are in the safe house the leaders of the "rebels" decide to go out to a club and party. DESPITE SLOANE AND JAMES BEING WANTED FUGITIVES. DESPITE ALL OF THEM BEING ESCAPEES. THIS IS THE BEST IDEA EVER DUH.<br /><br />So of course drama happens and the "rebel" leader gets drunk and by this point of the book Sloane and James have made out AT LEAST fifteen times and almost had sex twice because that's ALL THEY DO because that's what you do when you're on the run I guess.<br /><br />And of course the club gets busted and they have to flee the "safe" house and Lacey disappears and somehow ends up back IN The Program even though we have no idea HOW she got found and then Sloane and James end up with the "rebel" leaders (who decide that the rest of the "rebels" should just go off and do whatever somewhere else because OH YEAH Sloane and James are SUPER WANTED and being around them isn't safe. DUHHHHHH! <br /><br />So then they go off to this countryside house or idek but they're just hanging out and the "rebel" leader is just... always on her phone. And 'doing stuff'. This 'stuff' is NEVER EXPLAINED. And basically I keep saying "rebels" because THEY NEVER ONCE DO ANYTHING REBELLIOUS. EVER. They just talk. And the leader and her BFF practice knife fighting and mysteriously have money whenever they need it and nothing happens. James and Sloane make out more and OOPS forget the condoms and actually talk about not having them so they can't have sex. Because again that's all you do when you're on the run.<br /><br />THEN Realm shows back up and caused love triangle drama because EVEN THOUGH Sloane and James have been ALL OVER EACH OTHER EVERY OTHER PAGE Sloane just ~cannot~ deny that there was ~something~ between her and Realm and even though she ~looooooves~ James so much she can't NOT admit that she ~cares about and missed~ Realm and she lets him basically get close enough to her that James thinks something is going on and OF COURSE this is bad enough that he has to freaking RUN AWAY and leave Sloane. That's REAL mature and shows JUST how much he loves her.<br /><br />So then there's a bunch of drama and Realm is SO FUCKING CREEPY GTFO OMG. And they go on the run again and finally get caught by The Program and by this point I was just SO sick of this book and SO bored and didn't want to read it anymore but I forced myself to because I was way past the DNF point and I wanted to see if it got better but it just GOT WORSE. So Sloane is back in the program and all of these BIG BAD AWFUL BOMBSHELLS are dropped and people are getting lobotomized and it was just like WHY. Why would this huge company put all of this money into making useless people. It just made no sense. Why waste money on something that is going to give you NO RETURNS. So Sloane is, of course, set to get a lobotomy but she, OF COURSE breaks out just as James and Realm are breaking in to save her and oh yeah, they HAVE A CURE that will bring back their memories, but there's only one pill left and for some reason it's SUPER EVIL and James takes it and then they go to find the scientists who made the pill but because even though The Program took away everyone's memories giving them BACK is bad too???????? WHICH IS IT?! jfc I just had no idea what this story was even trying to say.<br /><br />So blah blah blah Sloane and the scientists who made The Treatment talk to the press and then... THE PROGRAM IS RUINED. <br /><br />What.<br /><br />That's it?<br /><br />NOTHING HAPPENED.<br /><br />So if you're with me it was basically:<br /><br />Sloane and James make out<br />Realm is creepy and shows up<br />Love triangle ensures<br />Sloane is captured<br />Sloane is freed<br />Sloane tells the press<br />END OF ALL EVIL IS ACHIEVED<br /><br />There's also more making out. And by the end of the book James and Realm are BFFs. Cuz that makes even more sense.<br /><br />There was no rebellion. There was no real conflict. Sloane being back in the program was BORING AS FUCK to read and the resolution was just... so ridiculous. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17805456068254333973">This was an okay story, and there were some interesting twists.<br/><br/>Sloane and James were both on the run in this book, and still undecided if one of them should take the pill which will allow them to regain their memories.   <span id="freeText17805456068254333973" style="display:none">This was an okay story, and there were some interesting twists.<br /><br />Sloane and James were both on the run in this book, and still undecided if one of them should take the pill which will allow them to regain their memories. I could see where they were both coming from, but it really seemed like the odds were against them all the time.<br /><br />The storyline in this had a few twists which were good, but once again the pace was quite slow and it was a bit of a struggle to get through this. We did get some interesting information on both ‘the program’ and ‘the treatment’ in this story though, along with she very interesting questions raised over what would happen to the people who took ‘the treatment’ – would they all become suicidal again?<br /><br />We did get a little bit of romance in this one, but unfortunately things weren’t even running smoothly for Sloane and James in that respect.<br /><br />The ending to this again had a little bit of action, and we also got some surprise deaths and even some lobotomies in this book!<br />6 out of 10<br /></span>

<div id="review_826825219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826825219" />
    <a title="Jenni Arndt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6971133-jenni-arndt"><img alt="Jenni Arndt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364785651p2/6971133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826825219?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenni Arndt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenni Arndt" href="/user/show/6971133-jenni-arndt">Jenni Arndt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6971133-jenni-arndt?shelf=arc-own">arc-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826825219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16322948337167667356">There’s always something nerve wracking about going into the sequel to a book that you loved. I was a huge fan of The Program so my hopes were high that The Treatment would follow in it’s awesome footsteps. I am saddened to report that it really didn’t. This novel fell so flat with me that I almost DNFed it about 3 times. But then I would think about how much I loved The Program and how since this is a duology this was the last book in the series and I just had to see how everything played out.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText16322948337167667356" style="display:none">There’s always something nerve wracking about going into the sequel to a book that you loved. I was a huge fan of The Program so my hopes were high that The Treatment would follow in it’s awesome footsteps. I am saddened to report that it really didn’t. This novel fell so flat with me that I almost DNFed it about 3 times. But then I would think about how much I loved The Program and how since this is a duology this was the last book in the series and I just had to see how everything played out.<br><br>I’ll start this out by talking about what didn’t work for me because the beginning was just a train wreck in my eyes and then the novel started to get better in the final part. The Treatment is broken up into 3 parts, in the first two we catch up with James and Sloane as they are on the run from The Program and join the rebels out in the wild. I remember loving Sloane and James’ relationship in the first novel but it was so over the top and cheesy in this one. Every moment between them felt like the sweetness was just laid on far too thick, so much so that I started to be annoyed by them instead of buying into their romance. Things get even worse when Michael Realm makes his reappearance and we are treated to one of the most annoying love triangles I have ever read. James becomes an annoying, whiney baby and Sloane loses who she is by flip flopping between the two in a matter of moments. I mean there are no doubts in my mind that she wanted James, and only James all along, but she would allow Realm to kiss her hand, or hold her hand and think about the love she has for him and it was so annoying!<br><br>Another thing that annoyed me was the lack of detail as to how the rebels were surviving and living the life that they were. Dallas had a cell phone that she was constantly on, no talk of her buying minutes or paying a monthly bill so I wonder how the heck she was always using it. Also, driving these vehicles all around the countryside, how were they paying for gas? At one point, when James is throwing his big temper tantrum, he takes the Escalade from the safe house and ends up driving for days. Where did he get money to keep going at that time? It was mentioned that Cas (one of the rebels) had connections to get money so maybe that would explain how they got money to buy information but James would not have had access to that when he was out on his own. Also, they go to all these abandoned places that have working power, running water and even hot water at that. Who is paying the bills at these places? For rebels on the run they lead a pretty cushy life and I would have liked some explanations as to how they have these luxuries at their fingertips.<br><br>Things do pick up in the final part of the novel. The action gets going and the twists start coming but as far as I’m concerned it was just too little too late. Also the final jab at the program that makes everything end the way that it does seems so trivial and simple that it makes the series feel like it went on for no reason if it all could have been ended by something so simple. I am so sad that the series is going out on such a negative note with me and I kind of wish I had not read this sequel so I could have remembered The Program much more fondly, but unfortunately I can’t unread this one. I do hope that other readers aren’t as annoyed as I am by these things and maybe my word of warning will help you go in with a bit of trepidation so you come out liking it more than I did.<br><br>--<br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388709049i/7906415.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16322948337167667356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Just know that James and Sloane and Realm are the focus of the story and there are a few familiar faces that reappear along side new ones. The Treatment wraps up all the loose ends from The Program and gives readers both a chapter six months after the main action of the book and an epilogue. This reader appreciates the decision to end the series in two books instead of manufacturing ext</span>
  <span id="freeText8065960285595058525" style="display:none">Such an amazing book! This reader isn't going to spoil the book for those waiting with spoiler laden synopsis. Just know that James and Sloane and Realm are the focus of the story and there are a few familiar faces that reappear along side new ones. The Treatment wraps up all the loose ends from The Program and gives readers both a chapter six months after the main action of the book and an epilogue. This reader appreciates the decision to end the series in two books instead of manufacturing extra drama and stretching out over three books. Eagerly awaiting whatever Mrs. Young decides to write next!</span>

I'm disappointed with this book. I mean, don't get me wrong here, this book still had some interesting moments here and there, but honestly what the hell happened to the awesomeness that I experienced from the first book???<br><br>With the first book I was all like this . . . <br><br><a href="http://s1109.photobucket.com/user/Erin_Woodbridge/media/Album%203/tumblr_n6ecvcLSAZ1r3wsyqo3_250_zps8bce9f81.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1036049651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036049651" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036049651?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036049651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12971501043623846876"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"I won't lose you, Sloane," he whispers. "I'll kill him if I have to."<br/>"I'd rather die."<br/>Realm turns away. "That's what I'm afraid of."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I'm mixed on this one-right up front I'll say that I contemplated quite a bit on what to rate this because I felt like there were two different paces of story going on. Or maybe it's the fact that I got to read the first half in one chunk so all the emotions were raw and natural whereas the whole second half I was forced to read in bits and pieces wh</span>
  <span id="freeText12971501043623846876" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"I won't lose you, Sloane," he whispers. "I'll kill him if I have to."<br>"I'd rather die."<br>Realm turns away. "That's what I'm afraid of."</i>
</b><br><br>I'm mixed on this one-right up front I'll say that I contemplated quite a bit on what to rate this because I felt like there were two different paces of story going on. Or maybe it's the fact that I got to read the first half in one chunk so all the emotions were raw and natural whereas the whole second half I was forced to read in bits and pieces when I got the time to do so. Regardless, my feelings are mixed for whatever reason and there was just <i>something</i> that kept me from making it a solid five star. <br><br><b>We're addicted to each other-no matter what the consequences.</b><br><br>Maybe, upon further inspection, there were many reasons why I gave this a 4.5, the main one being that at the end I never really felt like they weren't going to make it. I won't say how it ends, obviously, but I wanted a little more suspense and maybe a lot more angst. I know, right? How much more angst could this author have shoved into the story? But, and I can't believe I'm going to say this, I needed that angst from the first book/the first half of this book to continue to the end of it all. I know for a fact that it was loud when I was reading, it was annoyingly difficult to focus on the words forming before me, that it inevitably altered my reading experience-and that sucks. I will never know what it felt like to be fully immersed at the finale of this wonderful series. But who has the time (or the willpower to fight tired eyes) to wait until the house is dark and quiet? I sure don't. So, that effected the end <b>a ton.</b> And that little fact broke my heart. But, let me tell you, the first half of this book?? It's <b>Phenomenal.</b> The tension was so thick in the beginning half of this book you could cut it with a knife. I had butterflies, I had doubts, I had fears, I was scared to death for them and <b>I physically couldn't breathe.</b> Literally. I was so into this story that I was choking on butterflies, pulling my hair out in frustration and aggravation. I found that the beginning was completely on par with what I expected as a companion to book one, and for that I could rate no less than above. It earned those stars even if the end was sub par to my perilistic expectations.<br><br><b>I realize he's the biggest liar I've ever known. But he does it with the best of intentions.</b><br><br>I must say this now: James was off the charts sweet and completely, utterly, <b>madly</b> in love with Sloane. If there's one thing this author excels at, it's the beautiful and heartbreaking relationships she built in this story. If I had to sit and take out all the bad stuff, all the things that made this dystopian and action filled and read it only as a romance novel...I'd do it with absolutely no hesitation whatsoever. It's raw, it's beautiful and it completely ripped my heart out more than once even as Sloane and James ride along on this journey together. There were some hiccups that didn't need to happen I'm sure, but it only added the angst I was talking about and made me feel giddy and breathless as James fought to make Sloane his and only his....and to make sure they even had a forever to pursue. <br><br><b>James puts his hand on my cheek and turns me toward him; his touch is gentle, so serious. When I meet his eyes, my body relaxes slightly. James draws me into a hug, resting his chin on the top of my head, his arms tight around me.<br>"It's just us," I whisper into the fabric of his shirt. "Forever, just us."</b><br><br>I'm skeptical as to what I think should have happened to end this series (The addition of a third book or end it on book two as it did). On the one hand, I was happy to see this author didn't fall into the 'trilogy hype.' Not everything needs to be drug out for three installments. But, on the other hand, I can see where she would have benefitted from having an extension after this story. In the end, it did seem a tad rushed. More so when 'the final battle' came to pass. The end end (eleven weeks after, epilogue) was awesome. I loved both of the final chapters. But, leading up to these final moments, I missed some of the grit that could have been added to make it more dangerous and, I'll admit it, peril-filled. There's a fine-line between dragging something out and stunting the growth before it's fully developed, and I do think she made the right decision, albeit a little rushed. I mean, how many more horrifying events can these teens tromp through before they go even crazier??<br><br><b>"Human beings are cruel creatures. And what we don't understand, we tamper with until we destroy it."</b><br><br>I adored this series. I adored these characters. I lost countless nights of sleep due to the imminent doom these guys continually faced....and I loved every minute of it. <i>The Program</i> is by far the strongest installment for sure with it's devastating occurrences and star-crossed love between James and Sloane, but as a whole, this series is unforgettable and I'm so ecstatic I finally decided to read these. So now I will go order the hardbacks to add to my ever-growing collection, and I can't wait to come back and read them again and again...their love is just <b>that</b> addicting. <br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12971501043623846876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1028036793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1028036793" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19112398-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460236247p2/19112398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028036793?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/19112398-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442445833" href="/book/show/13260666-the-treatment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=totally-saw-it-coming">totally-saw-it-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=positive-surprise">positive-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=underrated-gems">underrated-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=dystopia-utopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-utopia-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19112398-sarah?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028036793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7958869778118688062">Imagine this.<br/>You live in a world similar to ours, with one exception: Suicide is an epidemic. If you show any signs of depression, you will be taken into the Program. <br/>They will strip you off your memories and personality until you are nothing but an empty shell of a human being. <br/>You will be rid of your passions, the people you love and completely disconnected from your old life. The doctors are passive-agressive and put on forced smiles and calm you down, to put a shot in your arm the next momen</span>
  <span id="freeText7958869778118688062" style="display:none">Imagine this.<br />You live in a world similar to ours, with one exception: Suicide is an epidemic. If you show any signs of depression, you will be taken into the Program. <br />They will strip you off your memories and personality until you are nothing but an empty shell of a human being. <br />You will be rid of your passions, the people you love and completely disconnected from your old life. The doctors are passive-agressive and put on forced smiles and calm you down, to put a shot in your arm the next moment. <br />Once you’re in, you never get out. <br /><br />Sounds like a far-fetched idea, right? One that's not too serious and only wants to be original, but actually makes no sense? <br />Think again.<br /><br /><u>5 reasons why you should read this duology:</u><br /><br /><b>#1 Brain-washing.</b> It’s a dystopian, so who wouldn’t expect manipulation to be such a big part of the story?<br />Young perfectly captures that cold, clinical and impersonal feeling of this world. The world-building is very simple, but this is not a story about the science and technology like many from the genre. <br />The concept of these books sounds bizarre, but portrays mental illness in a delicate way that isn’t pushy or looking for pity. <br />There’s no obvious antagonist to point fingers at, which makes this war even more difficult to fight. It is not a story of good and bad, but about the grey areas and blind belief in what you’ve been taught. <br /><br /><b>#2 Character-driven dystopia.</b> Hell to the yes.<br />The characters are what makes this duo shine. These people are so well-written, relatable and lovable. The book is full of desperation and grief, and the author weaves a compelling story starring some of the most heartfelt and realistic characters I've seen in this genre.<br /><br /><b>#3 It’s a very addicting read that I flew through.</b> The writing is straight-forward, with fast pacing and a plot where the stakes get higher and higher. I couldn’t turn the pages quickly enough.<br /><br /><b>#4 Fantastic relationships.</b> Sloane and James have known each other for a long time, so we skip that awkward fumbling and angst. They are so comfortable with each other, with huge chemistry and wit. Their dialogue is clever and funny and light up the otherwise dark tone. <br />There are some lovely friendships here as well.<br /><br /><b>#5 No second-book curse.</b><br />This series remains steady and well-written all the way through. Every new character we meet is well-rounded and adds something exciting to the story. It follows the typical dystopia concept, with a twist.<br />I love my strong duos, and everything is neatly wrapped up in this book. It’s bittersweet; we know they’ll never get back the people they’ve lost to this epidemic and things aren’t magically solved. But then again, this isn’t your typical dystopian. It is now my favorite after Julie Kagawa's Blood of Eden trilogy. <br /><br />I had a few quibbles with this sequel like the pacing of the first half and the predictable plot, but this was so entertaining that I could look past those cons. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[P.S: I would trade a whole chocolate bar for a novella about Sloane and James having a picnic; that's how much I like them together. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="7958869778118688062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2511936634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511936634" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10479935-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479130525p2/10479935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511936634?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/10479935-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36353058-the-treatment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10479935-diana?shelf=discarded-shelf">discarded-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511936634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13578167201431901367">My review of "The Program" series will be live on December, 25th, 2019 here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/MyVFNNOc32g'>https://youtu.be/MyVFNNOc32g</a><br/><br/><br/>3'5★<br/>The first time I began reading it I DNF'ed the book.<br/>This 2nd time I actuly devoured it, finishing it in a day. There are still moments that for me are cringe-worthy concerning the personal relations described on the book, i.e. how Realm can be such an ass and be forgiven every time or have Sloane chosing not to remember things so they can hold a truce, or how Dallas needs Realm's validati</span>
  <span id="freeText13578167201431901367" style="display:none">My review of "The Program" series will be live on December, 25th, 2019 here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/MyVFNNOc32g">https://youtu.be/MyVFNNOc32g</a><br /><br /><br />3'5★<br />The first time I began reading it I DNF'ed the book.<br />This 2nd time I actuly devoured it, finishing it in a day. There are still moments that for me are cringe-worthy concerning the personal relations described on the book, i.e. how Realm can be such an ass and be forgiven every time or have Sloane chosing not to remember things so they can hold a truce, or how Dallas needs Realm's validation, even at the end. I mean, it's cool to have someone to care for you, but it's vetter than you can do the fighting and validation yourself. The book was written on 2014, so I am thinking this is the kind of books which were common back then, and now we have stronger female leads, which I honestly prefer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13578167201431901367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2947208831" />
    <a title="Diabolica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39353094-diabolica"><img alt="Diabolica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465869709p2/39353094.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2947208831?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diabolica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diabolica" href="/user/show/39353094-diabolica">Diabolica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36353058-the-treatment">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947208831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12751524397722563496">The ending doesn't really make a whole lot of sense. Will I say it was rushed? <br/><br/>Absolutely, it came a lot faster and more abruptly than I thought possible, with the help of a seemingly deux ex machina. <br/><br/>But this book has made me selfish, and I cannot complain with the results. Given that this is, as I care to classify, an action-romance novel, there was quite a bit of action and in most romantic novels the happily ever after is always desirable. So when Young left us with a happily ever after, who</span>
  <span id="freeText12751524397722563496" style="display:none">The ending doesn't really make a whole lot of sense. Will I say it was rushed? <br /><br />Absolutely, it came a lot faster and more abruptly than I thought possible, with the help of a seemingly deux ex machina. <br /><br />But this book has made me selfish, and I cannot complain with the results. Given that this is, as I care to classify, an action-romance novel, there was quite a bit of action and in most romantic novels the happily ever after is always desirable. So when Young left us with a happily ever after, who am I to complain. <br /><br />I'm admittedly still confused the epilogue in the first novel where Realm messes up Sloane's name calling her Allison, but that's an end I don't really need tied up. <br /><br />I will say though, I am explicably happy that this duology ended, with the ends (at least the ones I was concerned with) nicely wrapped up. I was about to go read the third book should there be one for me to find the end I wanted. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12751524397722563496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2947208831'><a id="like_count_review_2947208831" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2947208831?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">9 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F17948607-the-treatment">Like</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_848459106" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848459106" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17389678-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145890p2/17389678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/848459106?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/17389678-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=the-dystopian-lot">the-dystopian-lot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=mw">mw</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer848459106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11937668043364481318"><i>The Treatment</i>, meet you’re extended kin: <b>The conventional, and overextended YA dystopia family</b>. <br/><br/>I’ve pretty much lost the plot by now. If you say read a YA dystopia, most likely I'll grant you a “bleh” in return. The dystopia and I were alright; friends, acquaintances, call it what you will. The relationship was amicable. Until only one side was giving it their all (shocker here guys, that side was me) and the other just cruised by, taking our friendship for granted. I ain’t stupid. I know when </span>
  <span id="freeText11937668043364481318" style="display:none"><i>The Treatment</i>, meet you’re extended kin: <b>The conventional, and overextended YA dystopia family</b>. <br /><br />I’ve pretty much lost the plot by now. If you say read a YA dystopia, most likely I'll grant you a “bleh” in return. The dystopia and I were alright; friends, acquaintances, call it what you will. The relationship was amicable. Until only one side was giving it their all (shocker here guys, that side was me) and the other just cruised by, taking our friendship for granted. I ain’t stupid. I know when you’re feeding me the same formula. And as we were friends, I’m going to lay it to you nicely:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> If you’re just going to be repackaged (in an ugly cover, no less) then please stop selling your multiple selves to me. One relationship will do. Don't take it beyond it's worth. </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I want integrity, ingenuity, and inspiration. I got<b> “You may remember me from such dystopias such as <i>Legend, Delirium…</i>”</b>* (Yes, do the <u>Troy McClure</u> voice, please).<br /><br /><i>The Treatment</i> was a fairly bumpy ride for me. I preach realism like it’s going out of fashion. While I personally believe that the plot is irrational, it does make a valid attempt at justifying it’s dystopian world. It’s not perfect, and probably forgets to factor in the rest of fucking humanity, but it’s a <b>cute</b> attempt. However, what this book managed to do is create a dystopia that exists <b>logically</b> in society. It’s nothing highly implausible such as oppressing human traits (you know who you are), or creating a state of enslaved citizens who regress back to the prehistoric ages. <br /><br />Outside <i>The Program</i> life functions just the way it would; thriving with capitalism, sensationalisation, and the fear of the unknown. <b>It still maintains a lifetime of development</b> and it just fucking makes sense. <br /><br />Certain dystopias like to think that society is just going to take a beating lying down, give up all their knowledge, weapon and machinery like fucking wusses. We are humans; different, confusing and opinionated as hell (this review is a perfect case study), and as if we would allow ourselves to be subjugated by some Republic without a damn hard fight. What I loved about <i>The Treatment</i> is that <b>life goes on</b>. Newspapers still sell, dogs still get walked, and Wall Street still makes fucking money. So it was nice; an <b>unrealistic</b> dystopia in a <b>realistic</b> world. <br /><br />But it ends there. The writing is utterly typical of a YA dystopian. Short, concise, with lots of fucking rhetorical questions to portray the protagonist as they go through some metaphysical experience (thanks to the dystopia, I’ve come to hate the 1st POV). If the question has no answer, then I don’t have the time. Stop asking such questions like they mean jack shit. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> How can any rational human being inflict this on another? How can this happen in a civilised world?</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Here, Sloane. Let me give you a clue. <b>You don’t live in a civilised world.</b> If you did then parents wouldn’t let their fucking children be carted off, conditioned, and brainwashed just to live and breathe air. Civilitiy is to be given a choice and a chance. In this case choice is stripped and chance is measly. <br /><br />From memory there was a little humour snuck through, but don’t expect anything comedic—this dystopian world is based upon a <i>depression epidemic</i>.<br /><br />There were so many damn times when I cried, exasperated. Sloane is just so incredibly boring and pretty much sad all the damn time. And I couldn’t even fucking complain about it because the book is about a damn <i>depression epidemic</i>. I picked it up, I’ll deal with it. <br /><br />That doesn’t excuse Sloane from being a damn <b>special snowflake</b>. Damn the fucking love triangle. This book could have squashed that stupid idea in the first book, but what the fucking heck, go for it anyway. Who the fuck died and made Sloane an irresistible goddess. This book is just about her love story. <b>HER LOVE STORY</b>.<br /><br /><blockquote><i> Meet James, my childhood <b>hotty hot hotty</b> who is my soulmate forever and ever. <br />Even though we don’t remember what joined us together we were in love in our previous lives and that love will fucking transcend the boundaries of our completely jello memories and reunite us once more.<br />Realm, my bffl from the Program makes a return, and oh! He reminds me off that pill he gave me, and <b>only fucking me</b>, that promises to bring my memories back. Because I’m so important, naturally.<br />Oh Realm, stop giving me all those <b>longing gazes</b>. We used to be together, but we can’t. Because I love James like he’s the other fucking half of my soul. But I’ll tell you I love you anyway. Platonically. I don’t mind leading you on even though I clearly know where your feelings lie. I get a high out of being a bitch. <br />James, no, don’t go! There’s nothing between Realm and I! I was just teasing him, <b>baiting him for later</b>, you know. But I’ll always love you and forgive you, no matter what. <br />Realm saves my fucking arse a multitude of times. But fuck him, I want James. <br />Reunited with the love of my fucking life, and Realm means nothing. <br />Even though Realm risks his entire life for me, I could never TRUST him, let alone love him. <b>James, you are the only one for me.<b></b></b></i> </blockquote><br /><br /><b>Are you motherfucking kidding me?!</b><br /><br />First off, James does absolutely nothing for her (except arouse her, I suppose), and yet their love is undeniable. I’m not saying that Realm is some prince (and I’m highly insinuating that his damn infatuation with Sloane is unrealistic. She’s a fucking special snowflake and nothing about her justifies his kindness), but he might as well be, with all the slack and opportunities he presents to Sloane. <br /><br />He saves her, time and time again and yet she fucks him over in the end. I felt absolutely no connection to this fucking love triangle so in essence I didn’t get as passionate. I did get angry, however, at the utter stupidness (way to go Jess, you're so literate) of the whole thing. There is this thing called <b>gratitude</b> and Sloane should consider getting some. I don’t want them to fall in love. I want none of that. What I <b>do</b> want is for her to respect and acknowledge <b>all the fucking chances he has given her.</b><br /><br />But instead, we get this:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> I’ve never been able to trust Realm again, and I don’t know if I ever will. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Just brilliant Sloane. Sloane is the kid at Christmas who makes a beeline for the presents on Christmas Day. She expects a ridiculously expensive Barbie doll, only to get a beautifully handcrafted scarf made with love, effort and care from her Grandmother, and still she throws a fissy hit. She is ignorantly ungrateful. It’s James this, James that, or James nothing. <br /><br />News flash Sloane! Life doesn’t revolve around James. <br /><br />You couldn’t even say that Sloane and James compliment one another. They in no way make each other better. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “We’re going to keep the pill in case we change our minds later, right?”<br />“My thoughts exactly.”<br />“You’re so smart,” he whispers, and kisses me. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Not sure if serious, or if fucking with me. If that was being smart then I would fucking triumph Einstein. James meet <b>Common Sense</b>, Common Sense, meet James (but you’re better off staying far away from such stupidity). <br /><br />The thing is, this entire book lacked the minimum quota of common sense. Were you robbed, <i>The Treatment</i>? I’ll happily give you some of mine. <br /><br />James and Sloane are <b>scolded</b> merely for <b>standing out on the street for a little too long</b>. So it’s safe to assume that secretion is best used, right? Well wrong. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “So we’re on the run from The Program, but we’re going to a club?” James asks, pointing out the obvious flaw in this plan. “Why not just call the handlers ourselves and ask them to meet us there?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />What possesses these idiots into thinking that going out <b>at night</b> would solve anything? Don’t fucking believe every idiom there is. The dark of the night is not the equivalent to a fucking cloak. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “We don’t want to die, but it’s fun to explore our dark sides when the rest of the world is intent on burying it.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />That’s all fun and games, but you’re all fucking <b>rebels</b> who are being <b>hunted</b>. Their priorities are <b>misplaced</b>. James and Sloane can’t rendezvous in daylight, but come fucking night everyone’s begging them to lose their fucking inhibitions. What a fucking joke. It was such a sad attempt by the author to inject a plot wherever it was convenient, despite the fact that it made <b>no logical amount of sense</b>. <br /><br />The book revolves around <i>The Program</i> and it’s attempt to trace an elusive <i>Treatment</i> pill in order to destroy and blacklist it’s ingredients. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “If The Program finds the pill before we do…the formula will be lost. They plan to extract the ingredients, patent them, and make their production illegal” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Have we not learnt anything in our expansive time on earth? There’s this thing called <b>illegal trafficking</b> and criminal activity. If someone was fucking desperate to procure this pill, a fucking patent and a group of pretentious governmental dicks are not going to stymie them. Take the Prohibition of alcohol in the 20’s. That was like a free mass marketing plan on a fucking golden dish, served straight from the government. If something becomes illegal, it becomes more inciting. It’s inherent in the human to <b>desire what he can’t have</b>. <br /><br />Once again, like <b>all</b> YA dystopias, we have our rebels—working hard for their righteous cause. Liberation! Except they all secretly care more for self-preservation and that in itself conflicts with their cause. They <b>go nowhere</b> (which is not typical at all. I’ve got to get some icepacks for my eyes, because they’ve out rolled themselves). <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> We have to protect Lacey, because in this world, you can’t know who to trust. All we have is each other. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />And that, ladies and gents, is why rebellions <b>do not work</b>. A group preaching freedom and achieving rights selflessly cannot be derived out of a group motivated by selfishness. We get it. Stop trying to spin this idea like a rebellion could actually work (if you minus a deus ex machina, because God knows, that solves everything). <br /><br />Granted I was in quite the book slump, this was the only thing that could drag me out (not because of that quality, but mostly out of obligation. I mean, I read the damn first book. If time is wasted, it’s going to be done in entirety.) I have a heinous memory and I had vague notes written about the first book. But nothing serious. And I payed for it. Normally the short recap that comes in a sequel isn’t that welcomed by me, but I could have killed for one in <i>The Treatment</i>. I remembered close to <b>nothing</b>. All the characters had memory lapses, but the person with the biggest missing chunk? <b>Me.</b> <br /><br />*By no means am I comparing the exact plot to these certain books, but the essence is the same. Love triangle/problems, rebels, special snowflakes etc etc etc<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><blockquote>_________________________________</blockquote><br />Immediate review, post completion:<br /><br />That beautiful piece that I wrote about the <b>conventional YA dystopia</b> has gone. Shocker, I know. I was bloody damn proud of it. Relax, it'll arise once again, perhaps on my blog. Did you really think I would wash that beautiful half an hours worth of time down the drain? <br /><br /><i>The Treatment</i> began well (despite me missing a suspiciously large chunk of my memory). Hell, I was even going to break the three star and below cycle and give it a four. Until the last 20 pages where shit hit the fan, just for the sake of it. <b>Must we be drama queens?</b> I was going to praise you, <i>The Treatment</i> for doing what other dystopias fail to do—retain realism—and yet you got ahead of yourself, lost the plot and ended in the most convenient way possible. I guess the formula really is reverberant. There’s a better ending out there, but fuck it, let’s just end it conveniently. <br /><br />This isn’t my full review. It would be cruel for me to offload my frustrations onto this otherwise ok YA dystopia. If anything, this piece of anger belongs elsewhere. <b>A detailed review should be coming</b>. For now, have my satirical bitterness. Hopefully it should sate the onslaught of complaints I have. <br /><br />P.S. The rating is being considered. I don't feel that particular anger so its a three and above, but I don't feel the elation of a four either. I do like how the epilogue tied things together. Young does a <b>better job than most</b> at reaching for <b>all</b> her loose ends and tying them up into one big knot. Kudos.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11937668043364481318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327175344?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aisha" href="/user/show/7783425-aisha">Aisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327175344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18222170193743787656">The Treatment is the second book in The Program duology/trilogy? Someone clarify please!<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[In this world, suicide is a disease that is plaguing teens in the US (possibly worldwide). In order to combat this epidemic, The Program is implemented in order to save teens from taking their own lives. When people go into The Program, they are almost "reset" and the memories causing them pain and depression are erased. <br/><br/>In the first book Sloane and her boyfriend James (as well as her late brot</span></span>
  <span id="freeText18222170193743787656" style="display:none">The Treatment is the second book in The Program duology/trilogy? Someone clarify please!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In this world, suicide is a disease that is plaguing teens in the US (possibly worldwide). In order to combat this epidemic, The Program is implemented in order to save teens from taking their own lives. When people go into The Program, they are almost "reset" and the memories causing them pain and depression are erased. <br /><br />In the first book Sloane and her boyfriend James (as well as her late brother's best friend) are placed into the Program and "fixed". But fate brought them back together at the end of the first book and they ended up back together and are on the run. And that's where the second book picks up.<br /><br />Now that we are all caught up. This was an enjoyable book. It was definitely action packed and fast paced for the most part. At times, i found Sloane to be a bit immature and naive considering what she has been through, but I gave did cut her some slack since her memory was erased. I liked the introduction of other minor characters that ended up impacting the story in a major way. Pretty good read. Well written.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15876054674931710835">Bleh. This felt like a forced, unnecessary sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11366397.The_Program__The_Program___1_' title='The Program (The Program, #1) by Suzanne Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Program</a>. I loved that book and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22449285.The_Remedy__The_Program___0_5_' title='The Remedy (The Program, #0.5) by Suzanne Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Remedy</a> as well, but this book is giving me the same feeling as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25041504.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_' title='After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>After You</a> after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_' title='Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a>. It just doesn't add anything. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[And I dislike it that the epilogue of The Program is being ignored, I was very satisfied with that ending. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>I recommend The Program and The Remedy, I'm certainly going to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23666204.The_Recovery__The_Program___2_5_' title='The Recovery (The Program, #2.5) by Suzanne Young' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Recovery</a>, but I don't recommend this book.</span>
  <span id="freeText15876054674931710835" style="display:none">Bleh. <div id="review_816856703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816856703" />
    <a title="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm"><img alt="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423864239p2/24060858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816856703?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)" href="/user/show/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm">Charnell (Reviews from a Bookworm)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm?shelf=reviewed-on-blog">reviewed-on-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24060858-charnell-reviews-from-a-bookworm?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816856703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4711262851686434788"><i>Early ARC review</i><br/><br/>I first want to start off by saying that I love the pill cover, I think it works really well with the first book cover and ties in with the story. I thought the case cover was a really cool idea, like on the first book but I wasn't the biggest fan of the one for The Treatment. Now they're using it as the actual book cover and I'm even more disappointed.<br/><br/>Reviewing this book is really hard for me, especially since I loved the first book so much. But I can't lie, I was really disappo</span>
  <span id="freeText4711262851686434788" style="display:none"><i>Early ARC review</i><br /><br />I first want to start off by saying that I love the pill cover, I think it works really well with the first book cover and ties in with the story. I thought the case cover was a really cool idea, like on the first book but I wasn't the biggest fan of the one for The Treatment. Now they're using it as the actual book cover and I'm even more disappointed.<br /><br />Reviewing this book is really hard for me, especially since I loved the first book so much. But I can't lie, I was really disappointed by The Treatment. It wasn't a very satisfying ending and the rushed conclusion really left me feeling deflated and let down. As always, I will try to be as honest as possible and explain why this was without giving away spoilers.<br /><br />James and Sloane are now on the run, unwilling to let The Program find them and take away their memories. They must trust Realm and the rebels he leads them to, to keep them safe and to keep them out of The Program. The Treatment, a pill that can bring back the memories The Program took away, seems like the exact thing they need. But it's not that simple, memory recall can come with it's own problems. Do they really want to take it if it just makes them sick again?<br /><br />I thought the main storyline was really good and interesting, the idea that they could get their memories back really appealed to me. Sloane, without her memories, isn't anywhere near as likeable as the girl we met in book one. In fact, most of the time she was absolutely intolerable and infuriating and I wanted to hit the girl. My favourite character is still James. I thought he was brilliant in the first book and I really wish he had more time to shine in this. I also began to realise that I didn't like Sloane half as much when she wasn't around James, he definitely brings out her better side.<br /><br />Realm was one of the biggest issues for me when it came to this book. The whole forced love triangle just felt silly and really grated on me the entire book. I couldn't understand the way Sloane acted or why she had such strong feelings for Realm. If you've read my review of The Program you will know that I hate the guy. He is strange, manipulative and really creepy. He knew Sloane for about three weeks in The Program and is insistent that he is head-over-heels, would-die-for-her in love with her. That just makes zero sense and wound me up constantly. Every time I had to sit through another one of his speeches about how he loves Sloane more than James ever could, I was about ready to throw my Kindle across the room and give up entirely.<br /><br />The story moved along nicely and there was a lot going on. This did keep me guessing, which I enjoyed and I wasn't able to predict what was going to happen. I was a little bored at times but for the most part I thought it was a really entertaining sequel. I didn't want to put the book down, I had to keep turning the page which is always a good sign.<br /><br />Something that I didn't get from the book was answers. In the first book I didn't think the suicide epidemic was explained well enough. Why do hordes of teenagers suddenly start killing themselves? I was really upset that you don't get any real explanation to that in this book. It seems like suicide is just something teenagers start turning to as the answer to everything, or just because someone else did. I couldn't get over that, it seems so ridiculously silly to me. I feel it portrays suicide as some really flippant issue, and that teenagers are just hormonal, overly emotional people incapable of finding another solution to their problems. It doesn't work that way and I don't think it's good to show suicide or depression in that light. It makes the whole issue seem trivial. It was very 47 Ronin in that sense.<br /><br />The ending was way too rushed for my liking. And something that you would expect to have a whole chapter written for it, is actually just summed up in two or three paragraphs. It does have the added bonus of showing you what's happening six months later, which is always quite nice. But then adds on an epilogue that just didn't seem to fit. The rushed ending just made this all seem very anti-climactic and I was left unsatisfied. I didn't feel this packed the same punch as the first book, it fell a little flat for me.<br /><br />3/5 Stars<br /><br />Disappointing and anti-climactic rushed ending. Sloane isn't very likeable in this book, Realm is infuriating and James needed more time to shine. The love triangle was just way too much for me. A good book, but not the satisfying ending I was hoping for.<br /><br />*I received a copy of this novel from the author/publisher/publicist via Edelweiss in exchange for a free and honest review and received no monetary compensation for this review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4711262851686434788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/813667719?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dystoromance">dystoromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813667719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13758955760460379551">Quick review for a very sluggish read (on my part, even if it only took me a day, realistically speaking). I honestly didn't like "The Treatment" much at all, but I'm giving it credit for some moments that were harrowing enough for the characters to invest me in pursuing it to the end. The problem is that there really wasn't a lot happening in this book with respect to the central conflict. It begins where it leaves off - the promise of Sloane and James taking off and making their escape from th</span>
  <span id="freeText13758955760460379551" style="display:none">Quick review for a very sluggish read (on my part, even if it only took me a day, realistically speaking). I honestly didn't like "The Treatment" much at all, but I'm giving it credit for some moments that were harrowing enough for the characters to invest me in pursuing it to the end. The problem is that there really wasn't a lot happening in this book with respect to the central conflict. It begins where it leaves off - the promise of Sloane and James taking off and making their escape from the Program in order to find a way to take it apart and possibly recover their memories. Only this book is one example of the plot driving the characters rather than the characters driving the plot. The supposed love triangle is uber forced and the relationship drama is what takes center stage over any of the dystopian or hefty elements the story had to offer. It felt very weak in overarching delivery and emotion in places. It wasn't until after the first third of the book was over that I started to find my footing with the plot. Even then, it felt thinly drawn and mostly constructed for convenience. It was frustrating because I knew what was going to happen well before it happened and while I did applaud that certain characters were called out and realized for the crummy things they pulled, I still didn't feel as invested in the character journeys as I was hoping for.<br /><br />I may check into the companion novels, but while this book gave a definitive ending for the characters contained within, I wouldn't cite it as one of the more memorable YA dystopian series I've read. I can say I've read it once at least, but it doesn't make me want to pick it up again after the initial read.<br /><br />Overall score: 2/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13758955760460379551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie" href="/user/show/10194401-abbie">Abbie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254037607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16144495857669272414">The characters in this were okay again, and I did feel sorry for them at points, as it seemed like nothing was going their way. <br/><br/>I found this one to be slightly better than book one, but it still wasn't great. Just like the first one, the pacing was slow, which made the story drag at points. It wasn't quite as bad though as some of the events were quite interesting. <br/><br/>Overall, An okay sequel. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_17190935'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17190935-just-like-fate"><img alt="Just Like Fate" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1356888889l/17190935._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yRg/Nuk7P/xvj8J7/AszXfV2cBwJqmrXYhsQW9EVw8yREQYngKEsprcFQSnj38/CIacWsv41pDIIebaZ0lq6uw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('prGpslFvP3w7NkCTguIPVdK6cKAhrrEhUsPMNWMD+Sf+uJCjOPUsJuO8w8GdNvPKBmsWDtYxf8Q4oWr3YEyAUA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
